<a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_D" title="UK railway stations – D">D</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_E" title="UK railway stations – E">E</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_F" title="UK railway stations – F">F</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_G" title="UK railway stations – G">G</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_H" title="UK railway stations – H">H</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_I" title="UK railway stations – I">I</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_J" title="UK railway stations – J">J</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_K" title="UK railway stations – K">K</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_L" title="UK railway stations – L">L</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_M" title="UK railway stations – M">M</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_N" title="UK railway stations – N">N</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_O" title="UK railway stations – O">O</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_P" title="UK railway stations – P">P</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_Q" title="UK railway stations – Q">Q</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_R" title="UK railway stations – R">R</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_S" title="UK railway stations – S">S</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_T" title="UK railway stations – T">T</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_U" title="UK railway stations – U">U</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_V" title="UK railway stations – V">V</a> <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_W" title="UK railway stations – W">W</a> X <a href="/wiki/UK_railway_stations_%E2%80%93_Y" title="UK railway stations – Y">Y</a> Z</small></span></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><small>* Annual estimated passenger usage based on sales of tickets in stated financial year(s) which end or originate at Liverpool Lime Street from <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://orr.gov.uk/statistics/published-stats/station-usage-estimates">Office of Rail and Road statistics</a>. Methodology may vary year on year.</small></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Liverpool Lime Street</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Terminal_train_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Terminal train station">terminus</a> railway station, and the main station serving the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_City_Centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Liverpool City Centre">city centre</a> of <a href="/wiki/Liverpool" title="Liverpool">Liverpool</a>. Opened in August 1836, it is the oldest grand terminus mainline station still in use in the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> A branch of the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a> from <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">London Euston</a> terminates at the station, as does the original <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway" title="Liverpool and Manchester Railway">Liverpool and Manchester Railway</a>. Services from this station serve a wide range of destinations across England and Wales, with direct services to Scottish destinations to be reintroduced in autumn 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Having realised that their existing <a href="/wiki/Crown_Street_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Street Station">Crown Street Station</a> was too far away from the city centre, the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway" title="Liverpool and Manchester Railway">Liverpool and Manchester Railway</a> (L&amp;MR) commenced construction of the more central Lime Street Station in October 1833. Designed by <a href="/wiki/John_Cunningham_(architect)" title="John Cunningham (architect)">John Cunningham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Hill_Holme" title="Arthur Hill Holme">Arthur Holme</a>, and <a href="/wiki/John_Foster_(architect)" title="John Foster (architect)">John Foster Jr</a>, it was officially opened in August 1836. Proving to be very popular with the railway-going public, within six years of its opening, expansion of the station had become necessary. The first expansion, which was collaboratively produced by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Locke" title="Joseph Locke">Joseph Locke</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Turner_(iron-founder)" title="Richard Turner (iron-founder)">Richard Turner</a>, <a href="/wiki/William_Fairbairn" title="William Fairbairn">William Fairbairn</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Kennedy_(manufacturer)" title="John Kennedy (manufacturer)">John Kennedy</a>, was completed during 1849 at a total cost of £15,000 (equivalent to £1,530,000&#32;in 2018)<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>. During 1867, work upon a further expansion of Lime Street Station commenced, during which time the present northern arched train shed was built. Designed by William Baker and Francis Stevenson, upon completion, the train shed was the largest such structure in the world, featuring a span of 200 feet (61&#160;m), as well as the first to make extensive use of <a href="/wiki/Iron" title="Iron">iron</a>. During 1879, a second parallel southern train shed was completed.
</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail#Nationalisation_in_1948" title="British Rail">nationalisation of the railways</a> during 1948, Lime Street Station was the subject of various upgrades and alterations, installing new signalling systems in and around the station, a redeveloped concourse, along with the building of new retail and office spaces. In 1962, regular electric services between Lime Street and <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a> were officially started and in 1966, the station hosted the launch of its first <a href="/wiki/InterCity_(British_Rail)" title="InterCity (British Rail)">InterCity</a> service, which saw the introduction of a regular 100&#160;mph (160&#160;km/h) service between Liverpool and London. During the 1970s, a new urban rail network, known as <a href="/wiki/Merseyrail#Creation_of_Merseyrail" title="Merseyrail">Merseyrail</a> was developed, while all other long-distance terminal stations in Liverpool were closed, resulting such services being centralised at Lime Street for the whole city. In October 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Pendolino" title="Pendolino">Pendolino</a> service operated by private rail operator <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains" title="Virgin Trains">Virgin Trains</a>, introducing a faster service between Liverpool and London, was ceremonially unveiled at the station. During May 2015, the electrification of the former Liverpool and Manchester Railway's route was completed, as well as the line to <a href="/wiki/Wigan" title="Wigan">Wigan</a> via <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="St Helens Central">St Helens Central</a>.
</p><p>Lime Street Station is fronted by a large building designed in the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Renaissance Revival</a> style, the former <a href="/wiki/North_Western_Hotel,_Liverpool" title="North Western Hotel, Liverpool">North Western Hotel</a>, which has since been converted to apartments. Since the 1970s, the main terminal building has also provided direct access to the underground Lime Street <a href="/wiki/Wirral_Line" class="mw-redirect" title="Wirral Line">Wirral Line</a> station on the <a href="/wiki/Merseyrail" title="Merseyrail">Merseyrail</a> network. Between the 1960s and 2010, an office tower block named <a href="/wiki/Concourse_House" title="Concourse House">Concourse House</a>, along with several retailers, stood outside the southern train shed; these have since been demolished and new facilities built elsewhere. Lime Street is the largest and oldest railway station in Liverpool, and is one of 18 stations managed by national infrastructure maintenance company <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> During 2017, work commenced at Lime Street Station upon a £340 million remodelling programme. In <i>Britain's 100 Best Railway Stations</i>, written by columnist and editor <a href="/wiki/Simon_Jenkins" title="Simon Jenkins">Simon Jenkins</a>, Lime Street Station was one of only ten to be awarded five stars.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The original terminus of the 1830 <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_and_Manchester_Railway" title="Liverpool and Manchester Railway">Liverpool and Manchester Railway</a> (L&amp;MR) was located at <a href="/wiki/Crown_Street_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Crown Street Station">Crown Street</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Edge_Hill,_Liverpool" title="Edge Hill, Liverpool">Edge Hill</a>, to the east of and outside the city centre. However, even before Edge Hill had been opened, it was apparent that there was a pressing need for another station to be built, which would this time be closer to the city centre. Accordingly, during October 1833, the construction commenced on a purpose-built station at Lime Street in the city centre; the land was purchased from Liverpool Corporation for £9,000 (equivalent to £840,000&#32;in 2018).<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The means of connecting the new station to L&amp;MR's network came in the form of a twin-track tunnel, which had been constructed between Edge Hill and the site of the new Lime Street station a year prior to work being started on the station itself; during the construction effort, the tunnel was frequently used to transport building materials for the station onto the site. The station was designed by the architects <a href="/wiki/John_Cunningham_(architect)" title="John Cunningham (architect)">John Cunningham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Hill_Holme" title="Arthur Hill Holme">Arthur Holme</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_Foster_(architect)" title="John Foster (architect)">John Foster Jr</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Echo-20120407_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Echo-20120407-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roscoe_GJR(1839)_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Roscoe_GJR%281839%29_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg/220px-Roscoe_GJR%281839%29_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Roscoe_GJR%281839%29_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg/330px-Roscoe_GJR%281839%29_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/10/Roscoe_GJR%281839%29_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg/440px-Roscoe_GJR%281839%29_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2208" data-file-height="1294" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Roscoe_GJR(1839)_p155_-_Entrance_to_the_Railway_Station_at_Liverpool.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A period depiction of the original Lime Street Station frontage circa 1839</div></div></div>
<p>During August 1836, Lime Street Station was officially opened to the public,<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> although the construction process was not completed until the following year. This building was designed with four large gateways, two of which were intentionally nonfunctional.<sup id="cite_ref-Echo-20120407_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Echo-20120407-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ItsLiverpool_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ItsLiverpool-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> For its early operations, as a consequence of the steep incline uphill from Lime Street to Edge Hill, trains would be halted at Edge Hill and the locomotives detached from the trains; the practice of the era was for the passenger carriages to be taken down by <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">gravity</a>, during which the rate of descent would be controlled by <a href="/wiki/Brakeman" title="Brakeman">brakemen</a> located in a brake van. The return journey was achieved via the use of a stationary <a href="/wiki/Steam_engine" title="Steam engine">steam engine</a> located at Edge Hill, which would be used to haul the carriages up to Edge Hill by rope. This system was constructed by the local engineering firm <a href="/wiki/Mather,_Dixon_and_Company" title="Mather, Dixon and Company">Mather, Dixon and Company</a>, who worked under the direction of the engineer <a href="/wiki/John_Grantham" title="John Grantham">John Grantham</a>. During 1870, this practice came to an end; instead, trains would enter and depart the station via conventional means.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_expansion">Early expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Early expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Lime Street Station was a near-instant success with the railway-going public. Within six years of its opening, the rapid growth of the railways had necessitated the expansion of the original station. An early plan for the enlarged station would have involved the erection of an iron roof, similar to that found at <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">Euston station</a> in London, which was a ridge roof supported by iron columns. However, a different proposal quickly gained the approval of the station committee. A single curved roof was produced by a collaborative effort; designed and <a href="/wiki/Load_testing" title="Load testing">load tested</a> by engineer <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Locke" title="Joseph Locke">Joseph Locke</a>, with construction contracted to <a href="/wiki/Iron_founder" title="Iron founder">iron founder</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Turner_(iron-founder)" title="Richard Turner (iron-founder)">Richard Turner</a>, and the work checked by engineer <a href="/wiki/William_Fairbairn" title="William Fairbairn">William Fairbairn</a> and manufacturer <a href="/wiki/John_Kennedy_(manufacturer)" title="John Kennedy (manufacturer)">John Kennedy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ET-LSSR_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ET-LSSR-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LA_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> The expansion work was performed at a cost of £15,000 (equivalent to £1,530,000&#32;in 2018)<sup id="cite_ref-inflation-UK_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-inflation-UK-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> and was completed during 1849, by which time the noted architect <a href="/wiki/William_Tite" title="William Tite">William Tite</a> had also been involved.<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Meanwhile, during 1845, the L&amp;MR had been absorbed by its principal business partner, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Junction_Railway" title="Grand Junction Railway">Grand Junction Railway</a> (GJR); the following year the GJR became part of the <a href="/wiki/London_and_North_Western_Railway" title="London and North Western Railway">London and North Western Railway</a>. Amongst the features which date back to the 1846–1849 rebuild of the station are a group of four columns which adjoin former Platform 1, they have been attributed to engineer <a href="/wiki/Edward_Woods_(engineer)" title="Edward Woods (engineer)">Edward Woods</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Sharples186_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharples186-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By 1857, a pair of <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> columns had been erected outside the station entrance; over time, these had become known as the "Candlesticks".<sup id="cite_ref-Echo-20120407_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Echo-20120407-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEHerdman1968Plate_29_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEHerdman1968Plate_29-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> During 1867, further expansion of Lime Street Station was required to cope with operational demands; changes included the present northern arched train shed. Designed by William Baker and Francis Stevenson<sup id="cite_ref-Sharples185_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharples185-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;nb 1&#93;</a></sup> the train shed featured a span of 200 feet (61&#160;m), leading to it being recognised as the largest such structure in the world at the time.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> It was also the first train shed in which iron was used throughout. During 1879, a second parallel southern train shed was completed, which had been designed by Stevenson and E.W. Ives.<sup id="cite_ref-Sharples185_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharples185-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> This second train shed featured dry construction techniques,<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;nb 2&#93;</a></sup> while each bay reportedly took only three days to build.<sup id="cite_ref-LA_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LA-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;nb 3&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg/220px-Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg/330px-Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg/440px-Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_3_Lime_Street_Station_2025960.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Inward view of Liverpool Lime Street Station in 1959</div></div></div>
<p>Lime Street Station is fronted by a large building, built in the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_Revival_architecture" title="Renaissance Revival architecture">Renaissance Revival</a> style, which formerly housed the <a href="/wiki/North_Western_Hotel,_Liverpool" title="North Western Hotel, Liverpool">North Western Hotel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Designed by <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Waterhouse" title="Alfred Waterhouse">Alfred Waterhouse</a>, the building was built during 1871 and served as student accommodation for <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_John_Moores_University" title="Liverpool John Moores University">Liverpool John Moores University</a> from 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> It was announced on 28 September 2018 that the building will be restored as a hotel by the Marcus Worthington Group at a cost of £30m. It will reopen as the Radisson RED Liverpool Hotel in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As a result of the <a href="/wiki/Railways_Act_1921" title="Railways Act 1921">Railways Act 1921</a>, which grouped the majority of railway companies together to create the <a href="/wiki/Big_Four_(British_railway_companies)" title="Big Four (British railway companies)">Big Four</a>, Lime Street Station passed into the ownership of the newly-formed <a href="/wiki/London,_Midland_and_Scottish_Railway" title="London, Midland and Scottish Railway">London, Midland and Scottish</a> (LMS) railway. The station played an early role in the development of <a href="/wiki/Travelling_Post_Office" title="Travelling Post Office">mail trains</a>, the <a href="/wiki/General_Post_Office" title="General Post Office">Post Office</a> first dispatched mail by train from Lime Street.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="British_Rail_era">British Rail era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: British Rail era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg/220px-Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg/330px-Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg/440px-Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lime_Street_from_St_George%27s_Hall_-_geograph.org.uk_-_147203.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The station's frontage seen in 2006, including the Concourse House tower block and a row of shops, which were demolished in 2009.</div></div></div>
<p>Upon <a href="/wiki/British_Rail#Nationalisation_in_1948" title="British Rail">nationalisation of the railways</a> during 1948, Lime Street Station became a part of the <a href="/wiki/London_Midland_Region_of_British_Railways" title="London Midland Region of British Railways">London Midland Region of British Railways</a>. On 28 January 1948, a new <a href="/wiki/Signal_box" class="mw-redirect" title="Signal box">signal box</a> controlling movements in and around Lime Street was commissioned; this signal box would remain in use for almost 70 years, being one of the last lever frames boxes still in operation by the time of its decommissioning during 2017-2018.<sup id="cite_ref-rail_engsig16_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rail_engsig16-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> During 1955, the station concourse was redeveloped and modernised.<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> During 1959, preparatory work commenced at Lime Street for the first stage of the electrification of the <a href="/wiki/West_Coast_Main_Line" title="West Coast Main Line">West Coast Main Line</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> On 1 January 1962, regular electric services between Lime Street and <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a> were officially started.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The railway lines to former platforms 10 and 11 were removed by 1965.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> On 18 April 1966, the station hosted the launch of its first <a href="/wiki/InterCity_(British_Rail)" title="InterCity (British Rail)">InterCity</a> service, which saw the introduction of a regular 100&#160;mph (160&#160;km/h) service between Liverpool and London.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 11 August 1968, the <i><a href="/wiki/Fifteen_Guinea_Special" title="Fifteen Guinea Special">Fifteen Guinea Special</a></i>, a return service to <a href="/wiki/Carlisle_railway_station" title="Carlisle railway station">Carlisle</a>, was hauled by the <a href="/wiki/LMS_Stanier_Class_5_4-6-0" title="LMS Stanier Class 5 4-6-0">Black Five</a> locomotive <a href="/wiki/LMS_Stanier_Class_5_4-6-0_5110" title="LMS Stanier Class 5 4-6-0 5110">45110</a> from Liverpool to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a> and back. Arriving back at Lime Street at 7:58 pm, this train marked the end of British Railways' final steam-hauled mainline passenger journey.<sup id="cite_ref-ItsLiverpool_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ItsLiverpool-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Merseyrail_Map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Merseyrail_Map.svg/220px-Merseyrail_Map.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="196" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Merseyrail_Map.svg/330px-Merseyrail_Map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/Merseyrail_Map.svg/440px-Merseyrail_Map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="660" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Merseyrail_Map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Merseyrail map in use until 2018, when <a href="/wiki/Maghull_North_railway_station" title="Maghull North railway station">Maghull North</a> was included. Lime Street is visible on the right-hand side of the central loop.</div></div></div>
<p>An office tower block named <a href="/wiki/Concourse_House" title="Concourse House">Concourse House</a>, along with a row of small retail outlets, used to stand outside the southern train shed, obscuring the arches. These dated from the 1960s, and by the 2000s had become run down.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> They were demolished as part of a comprehensive refurbishment completed in 2010.
</p><p>During the 1970s, a new urban rail network, known as <a href="/wiki/Merseyrail#Creation_of_Merseyrail" title="Merseyrail">Merseyrail</a> was developed, resulting in four terminus stations being taken out of use in Liverpool and Birkenhead centres.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;nb 4&#93;</a></sup> As a consequence of this restructuring and rationalization, only Lime Street remained as a terminus, thus serving as a central point for the whole region for medium- and long-haul routes. At the same time, the Merseyrail network provided commuters with ease of access across the whole Merseyside region to the one remaining large terminus.
</p><p>Between 1983 and 1984, the station concourse was again altered and refurbished at a total estimated cost of £7.4 million.<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Hansard19840430_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hansard19840430-45">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> This refurbishment included the construction of the black glass building which partially surrounds platforms inside the northern train shed, as well as the glass screen which separates the concourse from platforms inside the southern train shed.<sup id="cite_ref-Sharples186_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sharples186-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> The alterations also coincided with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/International_Garden_Festival" title="International Garden Festival">International Garden Festival</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hansard19840430_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hansard19840430-45">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> On 29 November 1984, the new development was officially opened by <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">Princess Anne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint noexcerpt Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NOTRS" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:NOTRS"><span title="Self-published primary source (February 2017)">better&#160;source&#160;needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Privatisation_era">Privatisation era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Privatisation era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Doddy_and_Bessie,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_(geograph_2973892).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Doddy_and_Bessie%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973892%29.jpg/220px-Doddy_and_Bessie%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973892%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Doddy_and_Bessie%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973892%29.jpg/330px-Doddy_and_Bessie%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973892%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Doddy_and_Bessie%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973892%29.jpg/440px-Doddy_and_Bessie%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973892%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Doddy_and_Bessie,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_(geograph_2973892).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Statues of <a href="/wiki/Ken_Dodd" title="Ken Dodd">Ken Dodd</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bessie_Braddock" title="Bessie Braddock">Bessie Braddock</a>, installed in 2009</div></div></div>
<p>On 20 October 2003, the new <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_390" title="British Rail Class 390">Pendolino</a> service operated by private rail operator <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains" title="Virgin Trains">Virgin Trains</a>, which introduced a faster service between Liverpool and London, was ceremonially unveiled in the presence of the company's founder and chief executive officer <a href="/wiki/Richard_Branson" title="Richard Branson">Richard Branson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Designed from the onset to be a <a href="/wiki/Tilting_train" title="Tilting train">tilting train</a>, it quickly replaced much of the previously-allocated locomotives and rolling stock used on the West Coast Main Line, namely the <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_86" title="British Rail Class 86">British Rail Class 86</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_87" title="British Rail Class 87">87</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_90" title="British Rail Class 90">90</a> <a href="/wiki/Electric_locomotive" title="Electric locomotive">electric locomotives</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Mark_2" class="mw-redirect" title="British Rail Mark 2">Mark 2</a> and <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Mark_3" title="British Rail Mark 3">Mark 3</a> coaching stock.<sup id="cite_ref-samath_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-samath-49">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Prior to this, the fleet had been first introduced into passenger services from <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_International_railway_station" title="Birmingham International railway station">Birmingham International</a> to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> on 23 July 2002 to coincide with the opening of the <a href="/wiki/2002_Commonwealth_Games" title="2002 Commonwealth Games">2002 Commonwealth Games</a> in Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>To help celebrate several high-profile occasions, such as Liverpool's role as <a href="/wiki/European_Capital_of_Culture" title="European Capital of Culture">European Capital of Culture</a> during 2008, and the city's 800th anniversary in 2007, a £35&#160;million redevelopment grant was issued for the station and its immediate surroundings. The Lime Street Gateway Project saw the demolition of the aging retail parade and office block located in front of the station, and an improved frontage and public plaza constructed in its place.<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Subsequently, Lime Street was voted <i>Station of the Year 2010</i> at the National Rail Awards.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The development was overseen by <a href="/wiki/English_Partnerships" title="English Partnerships">English Partnerships</a> and was completed in October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The main concourse features a pair of statues of comedian <a href="/wiki/Ken_Dodd" title="Ken Dodd">Ken Dodd</a> and politician <a href="/wiki/Bessie_Braddock" title="Bessie Braddock">Bessie Braddock</a>, a work entitled "Chance Meeting" by sculptor <a href="/wiki/Tom_Murphy_(artist)" title="Tom Murphy (artist)">Tom Murphy</a>, which were unveiled by Ken Dodd himself during June 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-plate_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plate-52">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On 31 August 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Earl_of_Wessex" title="Prince Edward, Earl of Wessex">Earl of Wessex</a> unveiled a memorial to the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_Pals" title="Liverpool Pals">Liverpool Pals</a> at the station. The memorial, which comprises two bronze friezes, was also sculpted by Tom Murphy.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> During 2014, former Platforms 1–5 were fully refurbished by national rail infrastructure maintenance company <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Electrification_to_Manchester_and_Wigan">Electrification to Manchester and Wigan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Electrification to Manchester and Wigan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Completion of electrification of the former Liverpool and Manchester Railway's route, and the line to Wigan via St Helens Central, during May 2015 led to a recast of timetables. This included the introduction of a brand new <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> service to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a> via Manchester Victoria, running alongside the existing service to <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a> via <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Central_railway_station" title="Warrington Central railway station">Warrington Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>. It was unclear whether suitable electric rolling stock would be available in time for the completion of the work,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> but it was confirmed during April 2014 that electric trains would be available to operate the new electric services, and the first trains were introduced from March 2015, initially on the service to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Airport railway station">Manchester Airport</a>, with services to <a href="/wiki/Wigan_North_Western_railway_station" title="Wigan North Western railway station">Wigan North Western</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Bank_Quay_railway_station" title="Warrington Bank Quay railway station">Warrington Bank Quay</a> following over the course of the year.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017_wall_collapse">2017 wall collapse</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2017 wall collapse">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>At around 17:45 on 28 February 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> the station was cut off after a wall collapsed into the cutting between Lime Street and Edge Hill,<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> causing more than 200 tonnes of debris to fall onto all four of the tracks running into the throat of the station.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc.co.uk_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc.co.uk-60">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> While the line was blocked, Virgin trains terminated at Runcorn and other trains terminated at Liverpool South Parkway.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The debris was cleared up, with repairs made to the overhead wires, and the station reopened just over a week later on 8 March 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="2017.E2.80.9318_station_remodelling"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2017–18_station_remodelling">2017–18 station remodelling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2017–18 station remodelling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg/220px-Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg/330px-Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg/440px-Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4160" data-file-height="2340" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Liverpool_Lime_Street_station_20181222_161656R.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Liverpool Lime Street Station at night in Dec. 2018.</div></div></div>
<p>During 2017, work commenced upon a £340 million remodelling programme intended to improve Lime Street Station by modernising its signalling systems, install new platforms, and other to better conform with current demands.<sup id="cite_ref-LE1_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LE1-65">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> A major impetus for the work was the age of the station's signalling, the core of which dated from the 1940s and was increasingly difficult to acquire knowledgeable staff for its operation and maintenance; furthermore, as resignalling of the existing station layout offered only slightly less work than the implementation of an entirely fresh layout, only without the benefits of being able to do so, it was decided to take the rare occasion as a convenient chance to make various alterations and improvements at the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-rail_engsig16_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rail_engsig16-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Perhaps the most noticeable change made for the perspective of passengers was the creation of an additional pair of platforms, which were built in the large space available between Platforms 7 and 8 (now 6 and 9); all of the other platforms were also lengthened and widened as a part of this work.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-limestreetninedayrevamp_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-limestreetninedayrevamp-67">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg/220px-Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="63" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg/330px-Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg/440px-Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3592" data-file-height="1036" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Former_platforms_at_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_02.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The former "cab road", between former platforms 7 and 8 (now 6 and 9), which was replaced by two new platforms.</div></div></div>
<p>According to industry publication <i>Rail Engineer</i>, the old layout of the station was relatively complex and posed some operational difficulties; many of the alterations sought to ease or eliminate some of these issues.<sup id="cite_ref-rail_engsig16_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rail_engsig16-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> As the curving of Platform 6 (now 5) had been a source of long-term driver difficulty in maintaining signal sightings, the platform was reprofiled to be straighter, permanently ending the problem. The new layout provides five platforms on each side of the station; beyond being simpler, the change facilitates the departure speed being increased from 15 to 25&#160;mph and is also compatible with being maintained by modern mechanised equipment.<sup id="cite_ref-rail_engsig16_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rail_engsig16-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> In conjunction with the layout changes, new Mk3D <a href="/wiki/Overhead_line" title="Overhead line">overhead line</a> equipment was installed along the route between Lime Street station and Edge Hill. Control of the signalling was transferred over to the centralised <a href="/wiki/Rail_operating_centre#ROC_locations" title="Rail operating centre">Manchester Rail Operating Centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rail_engsig16_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rail_engsig16-34">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The remodelling of Lime Street had been deemed necessary in order to provide the capacity for additional services to Glasgow, which are set to start during 2019. Various new retail outlets, along with a <a href="/wiki/Supermarket" title="Supermarket">supermarket</a>, were also established by work performed during the programme.<sup id="cite_ref-LE1_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LE1-65">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> To accommodate the work, the station was mostly closed over a twenty-three day period, which started on 30 September 2017; during the latter stages of this blockade, limited services ran to/from Huyton and some destinations beyond this. The station closed from 2 June 2018 to 29 July 2018 to allow more of the remodelling to be undertaken.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Station_layout">Station layout</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Station layout">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Liverpool Lime Street is divided into two sections: the mainline station, which offers national inter-city and regional overground services including local <a href="/wiki/City_Line_(Merseyrail)" title="City Line (Merseyrail)">City Line</a> routes, and services on the Wirral Line on the Merseyrail network, located underground between the mainline station and <a href="/wiki/St_George%E2%80%99s_Hall,_Liverpool" class="mw-redirect" title="St George’s Hall, Liverpool">St George's Hall</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mainline_station">Mainline station</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Mainline station">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br /><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i>&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Liverpool+Lime+Street+railway+station%22">"Liverpool Lime Street railway station"</a>&#160;–&#160;<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Liverpool+Lime+Street+railway+station%22+-wikipedia">news</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Liverpool+Lime+Street+railway+station%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Liverpool+Lime+Street+railway+station%22+-wikipedia">books</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Liverpool+Lime+Street+railway+station%22">scholar</a>&#160;<b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Liverpool+Lime+Street+railway+station%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2018</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg/220px-North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg/330px-North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg/440px-North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="426" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:North_Western_Hotel_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1000304.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The station is fronted by the former <a href="/wiki/North_Western_Hotel,_Liverpool" title="North Western Hotel, Liverpool">North Western Hotel</a>, built in the Renaissance Revival style resembling a French Château.</div></div></div>
<p>The mainline station is still covered by the vast iron and glass roofs dating from the 1870s. Platforms 1 to 5 are shorter than 6 to 10, the latter dealing mainly with long-distance services to London, Birmingham, Leeds, Sheffield and Norwich. Access to platforms 1–5 is through a ticket inspection barrier similar to airport <a href="/wiki/Passport_control" class="mw-redirect" title="Passport control">passport control</a>, while former platform 7 was gated with the creation of new shops and facilities. Former Platforms 8 and 9 were still "open".
</p><p>In 2009, new buildings were erected in the old "cab road" area between former platforms 7 and 8. Until the 2018 station remodelling, these housed customer lounges, the Virgin Trains customer service point, and an ATM, and there were retail units which had coffee shops amongst the units.
</p>

<p>There were also four non-passenger tracks.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Three of these were <a href="/wiki/Headshunt" title="Headshunt">headshunts</a>, created in the northern trainshed to turn locomotives around: Track A, in between former platforms 1 and 2; track B, serving former platforms 3 and 4; and track D, for former platforms 5 and 6. There is also a platform with no passenger service between former platforms 6 and 7, known as platform E, or sometimes affectionately as platform 6¾.
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r905231330">.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery{display:table}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-default{background:transparent;margin-top:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-center{margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-left{float:left}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-right{float:right}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-none{float:none}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery-collapsible{width:100%}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .title>div{display:table-cell;text-align:center;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .main>div{display:table-cell}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .caption{display:table-row;vertical-align:top}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .caption>div{display:table-cell;display:block;font-size:94%;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .footer>div{display:table-cell;text-align:right;font-size:80%;line-height:1em}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallerybox .thumb img{background:none}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .bordered-images img{border:solid #eee 1px}.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .whitebg img,.mw-parser-output .mod-gallery .gallerybox div{background:#fff!important}</style><div class="mod-gallery mod-gallery-default mod-gallery-center"><div class="title"><div>The station interior and approach</div></div><div class="main"><div><ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional nochecker bordered-images" style="line-height:130%;">

<p>From Edge Hill, the Liverpool Lime Street Approach is a descent at a gradient of 1 in 88, covering a distance of 1&#160;mi 30&#160;ch (2.2&#160;km).<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Facilities">Facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Toilets, booking offices, shops, a left-luggage office, taxi ranks and coffee bars are amongst the facilities provided. The main booking office is operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>. The concourse of the station contains several shops, including branches of <a href="/wiki/M%26S_Simply_Food" class="mw-redirect" title="M&amp;S Simply Food">M&amp;S Simply Food</a>,  <a href="/wiki/Caff%C3%A8_Nero" title="Caffè Nero">Caffè Nero</a>, <a href="/wiki/Costa_Coffee" title="Costa Coffee">Costa Coffee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boots_UK" title="Boots UK">Boots</a> and <a href="/wiki/WHSmith" title="WHSmith">WHSmith</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Car parking is managed by <a href="/wiki/APCOA_Parking" title="APCOA Parking">APCOA</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-RT1_8-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RT1-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The station also has two taxi ranks.<sup id="cite_ref-NR1_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NR1-72">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_transport_links">Public transport links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Public transport links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The station has direct bus services to the <a href="/wiki/Liverpool_One_bus_station" title="Liverpool One bus station">Liverpool One bus station</a> on the 10A, C4 and C5 routes (<a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.merseytravel.gov.uk/about-us/Documents/Liverpool%20Review%20-%20Proposed%20Changes.pdf">Until July 2017</a>), and from the bus station for Liverpool John Lennon Airport use services 86A (frequent &amp; night services) and 500. The bus services are provided by <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_West" title="Arriva North West">Arriva North West</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Cumfybus" title="Cumfybus">Cumfybus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The main station is currently served by six train operating companies serving a wide variety of destinations, but the service has been much reduced in recent times. For example, it is no longer possible to travel directly to Edinburgh, Plymouth, Southampton and Cardiff without changing trains. Services out of Lime Street (as of May&#160;2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>) are as follows:
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158,_158799,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_(geograph_3819385).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158%2C_158799%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_3819385%29.jpg/220px-East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158%2C_158799%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_3819385%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158%2C_158799%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_3819385%29.jpg/330px-East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158%2C_158799%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_3819385%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158%2C_158799%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_3819385%29.jpg/440px-East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158%2C_158799%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_3819385%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:East_Midlands_Trains_Class_158,_158799,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_(geograph_3819385).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An East Midlands Trains <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_158" title="British Rail Class 158">Class 158</a> at former Platform 6</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="East_Midlands_Railway">East Midlands Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: East Midlands Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Railway" title="East Midlands Railway">East Midlands Railway</a> operate an hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Norwich_railway_station" title="Norwich railway station">Norwich</a> via <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Central_railway_station" title="Warrington Central railway station">Warrington Central</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Piccadilly railway station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>, <a href="/wiki/Stockport_railway_station" title="Stockport railway station">Stockport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sheffield_station" title="Sheffield station">Sheffield</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham railway station">Nottingham</a>. Late afternoon and evening services terminate or start at Nottingham.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="TransPennine_Express">TransPennine Express</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: TransPennine Express">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a> operates an hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_railway_station" title="Newcastle railway station">Newcastle</a> via <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leeds_railway_station" title="Leeds railway station">Leeds</a> and <a href="/wiki/York_railway_station" title="York railway station">York</a> as well as an hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Scarborough_railway_station" title="Scarborough railway station">Scarborough</a> which since May 2018 goes via the same route. Late services start or terminate at York and Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_350_EMU,_Lime_Street_Station,_Liverpool_(geograph_2974858).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Class_350_EMU%2C_Lime_Street_Station%2C_Liverpool_%28geograph_2974858%29.jpg/220px-Class_350_EMU%2C_Lime_Street_Station%2C_Liverpool_%28geograph_2974858%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Class_350_EMU%2C_Lime_Street_Station%2C_Liverpool_%28geograph_2974858%29.jpg/330px-Class_350_EMU%2C_Lime_Street_Station%2C_Liverpool_%28geograph_2974858%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Class_350_EMU%2C_Lime_Street_Station%2C_Liverpool_%28geograph_2974858%29.jpg/440px-Class_350_EMU%2C_Lime_Street_Station%2C_Liverpool_%28geograph_2974858%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Class_350_EMU,_Lime_Street_Station,_Liverpool_(geograph_2974858).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A London Midland <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_350" title="British Rail Class 350">Class 350</a> at former Platform 8</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="London_Northwestern_Railway">London Northwestern Railway</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: London Northwestern Railway">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Since May 2019, <a href="/wiki/London_Northwestern_Railway" class="mw-redirect" title="London Northwestern Railway">London Northwestern Railway</a> operate an hourly service to <a href="/wiki/London_Euston_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="London Euston railway station">London Euston</a> via <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_New_Street_railway_station" title="Birmingham New Street railway station">Birmingham New Street</a> and an hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Birmingham_International_railway_station" title="Birmingham International railway station">Birmingham International</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364,_platform_2,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_(geograph_4500641).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364%2C_platform_2%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_4500641%29.jpg/220px-Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364%2C_platform_2%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_4500641%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364%2C_platform_2%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_4500641%29.jpg/330px-Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364%2C_platform_2%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_4500641%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364%2C_platform_2%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_4500641%29.jpg/440px-Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364%2C_platform_2%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_%28geograph_4500641%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Northern_Electrics_Class_319_319364,_platform_2,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station_(geograph_4500641).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_319" title="British Rail Class 319">Class 319</a> at former Platform 2. The new electric services to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_railway_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Manchester Victoria railway station">Manchester Victoria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wigan_North_Western_railway_station" title="Wigan North Western railway station">Wigan North Western</a> were both officially timetabled from 17 May 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> under <a href="/wiki/Northern_Rail_(Serco-Abellio)" title="Northern Rail (Serco-Abellio)">Northern Rail</a>'s branding of <a href="/wiki/Northern_Electrics_(Northern_Rail)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Electrics (Northern Rail)">Northern Electrics</a>.</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern">Northern</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Northern">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a> is the main train operating company at Lime Street, operating the ticket office. Services include:
</p>
<ul><li>Half hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Oxford_Road_railway_station" title="Manchester Oxford Road railway station">Manchester Oxford Road</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Central_railway_station" title="Warrington Central railway station">Warrington Central</a>, most local stations)<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Central_railway_station" title="Warrington Central railway station">Warrington Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester Piccadilly</a>, limited stop)</li>
<li>Hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Blackpool_North_railway_station" title="Blackpool North railway station">Blackpool North</a> (limited stop)<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Half hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Wigan_North_Western_railway_station" title="Wigan North Western railway station">Wigan North Western</a> (via <a href="/wiki/St_Helens_Central_railway_station" title="St Helens Central railway station">St Helens Central</a>, all stations)</li>
<li>Hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Newton-le-Willows_railway_station" title="Newton-le-Willows railway station">Newton-le-Willows</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport</a>, all stations)</li>
<li>Hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Warrington_Bank_Quay_railway_station" title="Warrington Bank Quay railway station">Warrington Bank Quay</a> (via <a href="/wiki/Earlestown_railway_station" title="Earlestown railway station">Earlestown</a>, all stations)</li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Platform_7,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_(geograph_2973857).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Platform_7%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973857%29.jpg/220px-Platform_7%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973857%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Platform_7%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973857%29.jpg/330px-Platform_7%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973857%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Platform_7%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973857%29.jpg/440px-Platform_7%2C_Liverpool_Lime_Street_%28geograph_2973857%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Platform_7,_Liverpool_Lime_Street_(geograph_2973857).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Virgin Trains <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_390" title="British Rail Class 390">Class 390</a> at former Platform 7</div></div></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Virgin_Trains">Virgin Trains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Virgin Trains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Virgin_Trains" title="Virgin Trains">Virgin Trains</a> operate an hourly <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_390" title="British Rail Class 390">Pendolino</a> service to <a href="/wiki/Euston_railway_station" title="Euston railway station">London Euston</a> calling at <a href="/wiki/Runcorn_railway_station" title="Runcorn railway station">Runcorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stafford_railway_station" title="Stafford railway station">Stafford</a> (peak services call additionally at <a href="/wiki/Lichfield_Trent_Valley_railway_station" title="Lichfield Trent Valley railway station">Lichfield Trent Valley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamworth_railway_station" title="Tamworth railway station">Tamworth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nuneaton_railway_station" title="Nuneaton railway station">Nuneaton</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_railway_station" title="Rugby railway station">Rugby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes_Central_railway_station" title="Milton Keynes Central railway station">Milton Keynes Central</a> and <a href="/wiki/Watford_Junction_railway_station" title="Watford Junction railway station">Watford Junction</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport_for_Wales">Transport for Wales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Liverpool_Lime_Street_railway_station&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Transport for Wales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Transport_for_Wales_Rail_Services" title="Transport for Wales Rail Services">Transport for Wales</a> operate an hourly service to <a href="/wiki/Chester_railway_station" title="Chester railway station">Chester</a> via <a href="/wiki/Runcorn_railway_station" title="Runcorn railway station">Runcorn</a>, using the <a href="/wiki/Halton_Curve" title="Halton Curve">Halton Curve</a> with peak-hour extensions to <a href="/wiki/Wrexham_General_railway_station" title="Wrexham General railway station">Wrexham General</a>, as of May 2019.
</p>
